```
"Rick Smith" <rs847925@gmail.com> wrote in message 
news:1954f173-bc21-4fd5-86ea-390ab624873a@o14g2000vbo.googlegroups.com...
On Dec 30, 7:47 am, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
> In article 
> <f52bdb82-5a59-437d-88e5-7dcab2732...@d8g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>,
> Rick Smith <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote:

[snip]

The program is segmented with segment numbers 0 and 50 - 54, in order.
I have almost finished entering segment 51, which builds the table.
Perhaps, when I finish entering segment 52, I will have a better idea
how the table is used. But, like a mystery, it is fun thinking about
the possibilities. Maybe a hash table would be a good choice.

Rick,
  When you are working with old IBM COBOL source code with segments, do make 
certain that you check on the rules for "reffeshable" and pemantent 
segments - and the segment-limit clause, etc. You might want to check out:
  http://publibfp.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/igy3mg50/4.1.7

and look for several items related to segmentation.  When working with your 
"old" program you need to know if it was compiled with LANGLVL(1) or 
LANGLVL(2) to determine how some segmentation worked.  The former is 
"sorf-of" ANS'68 and the later is ANSI'74.
```

> Doug Miller wrote:
>> On 12/31/2011 6:24 PM, HeyBub wrote:

>>>> On 12/30/2011 9:06 PM, HeyBub wrote:
<snip>>
> Maybe I wasn't clear: A hex dump of the SOURCE CODE!
>
In the "olde dayse", (before Hex-literals) we would use full screen editors 
(or punch cards, or whatever) to put "non-printable" chacters into 
alphanumeric literals.  When you were working wth these, you HOPED for an 
online editor to be able to run "hex" on or off, so that you could see what 
was in the literals.  When working with a dump, you sure HOPED that it 
showed the hex value of what was in them.

Now, I will say, I have never worked with a "general" hex dumpof a procedure 
division source listing.  I hope the dump had the "printable" version to the 
side.
```

#### ↳ Re: Converting old IBM code to ANSI 85

- **From:** Rick Smith <rs847925@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-02T13:01:12-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<d9ab9f29-4b69-4ed3-bfc6-c27b13f3767c@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1cd2a4b3-c242-40a4-a3a4-68129794fbbd@z19g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Dec 29 2011, 4:12 pm, Rick Smith <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote:

[snip]

> Now, if I have done my "homework" correctly, the changes will
> be:
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>    "read-disk".

At the end of segment 51 is became quite clear that the
disk file was holding two distinct "tables". Furthermore,
they were being maintained as doubly-linked lists. Thus,
each time a record was added, it was necessary to update
a pointer in the previous record. With the direct access
file, this was "read-update-write"; but, for a relative
file, this needed to be "read-update-rewrite". Though
not a big problem, I determined that the number of records
would be less that 200, so I commented all the statements
related to the file, added a table of 200 records, and
changed the 'write-disk' and 'read-disk' procedures to
reference the table. The actual number for the data I used
was 129. Problem solved and thanks to all!
```

#### ↳ Re: Converting old IBM code to ANSI 85

- **From:** "Bill Klein" <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-02T22:38:45-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<tDvMq.297560$lT4.161572@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<1cd2a4b3-c242-40a4-a3a4-68129794fbbd@z19g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
Rick,
  What you are doing is convering the old IBM extension for handling 
(proprietary BDAM files to ANSI/ISO Standard RElative Files.
The place you want to look is in the current Migration Guide, at:
   http://publibfp.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr/BOOKS/igy3mg50/4.1.4.2.1

What you have listed seems "right" on a cursory look, but I would suggest 
you check out the manual to see what else might be needed.

It has been a LONG time sicne I worked with "native COBOL language for BDAM, 
but as I recall it did NOT include file status field support, so you probaby 
want to add that as well.

"Rick Smith" <rs847925@gmail.com> wrote in message 
news:1cd2a4b3-c242-40a4-a3a4-68129794fbbd@z19g2000vbe.googlegroups.com...
>I am entering a program from a source listing for conversion
> from IBM to Micro Focus. The SELECT clause is not compatible
…[66 more quoted lines elided]…
> for comments on this problem. So, any comments?
```

On Jan 2, 11:38 pm, "Bill Klein" <wmkl...@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
wrote:
> Rick,
>   What you are doing is convering the old IBM extension for handling
> (proprietary BDAM files to ANSI/ISO Standard RElative Files.

I actually looked at that guide, last week. You had mentioned it
in a post a few years back. The guide was not particularly
helpful to me because IBM's conversion product would migrate
the file to VSAM or require separating the file and code into
an OS/VS program and link to Enterprise COBOL using LE.

I also looked at the Micro Focus Compatibility Guide where
it recommended conversion to relative files, but provided no
specific information reguarding the conversion of ACTUAL KEY
to RELATIVE KEY.

It was then I pulled out the old manuals to find what was
"really" required.

> What you have listed seems "right" on a cursory look, but I would suggest
> you check out the manual to see what else might be needed.

Having done the research, reviewed comments, and experienced
the effects of making the changes, I finally, as posted a few
hours ago, threw it all into a table!

<a id="t-9e9d895cd1"></a>
## Thread: "Abuse" of COBOL? — 26 msgs

### "Abuse" of COBOL?

- **From:** Rick Smith <rs847925@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-01T09:13:44-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com>`

```
The following program demonstrates a problem I encountered while
converting old IBM code to ANSI 85 for a computer that uses ASCII.
Of particular interest are lines 18 thru 21.

=====
      $set charset "ebcdic" badsigns apost
     1 identification division.
     2 program-id. hex-demo.
     3*Demonstrates 'abuse' of COBOL language on IBM <g>
     4 data division.
     5 working-storage section.
     6 01  hex-table value '0123456789ABCDEF'.
     7     03  hex-char pic x occurs 16.
     8 01  hex-value pic 99.
     9 01  cnt pic 9(4) comp.
    10 procedure division.
    11 begin.
    12     perform display-table
    13     varying cnt from 1 by 1
    14     until cnt > 16
    15     goback
    16     .
    17 display-table.
    18     move 0 to hex-value
    19     move hex-char (cnt) to hex-value (2:1)
    20     if hex-char (cnt) not numeric
    21         add 9 to hex-value
    22     end-if
    23     display quote hex-char (cnt) quote space hex-value
    24     .
===== [results for EBCDIC]
['0' thru '7' deleted as clear]
'8' 08
'9' 09
'A' 10
'B' 11
'C' 12
'D' 13
'E' 14
'F' 15
=====

Now, assuming that 'hex-value' (line 8) must be maintained
as is, what remediation is required to use ASCII characters?

I added the following similar code before line 21.
=====
               move function char (function ord (hex-value (2:1))
                   - function ord ("A") + 1 + function ord ("0"))
                   to hex-value (2:1)
===== [results for ASCII]
["0" thru "7" deleted as clear]
"8" 08
"9" 09
"A" 10
"B" 11
"C" 12
"D" 13
"E" 14
"F" 15
=====

The question then is: What are 'good', platform-independent
ways for converting hexadecimal characters to numeric values?
```

#### ↳ Re: "Abuse" of COBOL?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>

```
Rick Smith wrote:
> The following program demonstrates a problem I encountered while
> converting old IBM code to ANSI 85 for a computer that uses ASCII.
…[61 more quoted lines elided]…
> ways for converting hexadecimal characters to numeric values?

I can't see any "abuse" here, Rick.

It is a programming language; people use the facilities in it to do whatever 
they want. We may not always like what they do, but if the language allows 
it, then where is the "abuse"?

I would replace the entries in lines 6-8, as follows:

01 hex-table.
     12 filler   pic  x value "0".
     12 filler   pic 99 value 00.
...

     12 filler   pic  x value "F".
     12 filler   pic 99 value 15.
01  filler redefines Hex-table.
      12 namedPair occurs 16
                indexed by hex-ndx.
           15 Hex-char  pic x.
           15 Hex-value pic 99.

 A simple table with 16 entries would work on ANY COBOL platform without any 
need for intrinsic functions or complex, platform dependent arithmetic. (Not 
that I'm against intrinsic functions, but implementations do seem to 
vary...)

If you really wanted to, you could "refine" this to use SEARCH ALL.

Personally, if I need large scale Hex translation I simply use a component I 
wrote which translates a buffer of up to 8K from or to Hex. It has 
properties which allow various types of formatted results to be passed back.

If I actually needed to translate hex as you are describing I'd do it with a 
Regular Expression in line.

I have watched the original thread with some bewilderment.

Keying source data from a listing? Why? If the old system can produce a 
listing it can produce a file, and if the listing is ALL there is, then I'd 
be scanning it and reaching for an OCR engine.

I realise this is a bit of self indulgence on your part, but what if there 
were 100 such listings? Life's too short...

It isn't the "abuse" of COBOL you should be worrying about, it is the waste 
of your time....

Pete.
```

COBOL was intended to be platform independent with changes limited
to the ENVIRONMENT DIVISION. What I demonstrated was not; therefore
I find it reasonable to question whether it was "abuse".

Incidentally, after the change, the program works with either
EBCDIC or ASCII character sets.

> It is a programming language; people use the facilities in it to do whatever

maintained as is". That is, 'hex-value (sub)' is not the same as

>  A simple table with 16 entries would work on ANY COBOL platform without any
> need for intrinsic functions or complex, platform dependent arithmetic. (Not
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> If you really wanted to, you could "refine" this to use SEARCH ALL.

Well, no! SEARCH ALL will not work because the collating sequences
are different between ASCII (numbers before letters) and EBCDIC
(letters before numbers).

> Personally, if I need large scale Hex translation I simply use a component I
> wrote which translates a buffer of up to 8K from or to Hex. It has
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…

The system has long since been discontinued. IIRC, the system was
last used in 1979. The replacement system from 1979 to 1984. Its
replacement from 1984 to 1994. AFAIK, all that remains of the
original system is the listing. And, I don't have OCR available.

Incidentally, the data I am using is from the third system, 1988.
None of the original 'cards' are available either.

> I realise this is a bit of self indulgence on your part, but what if there
> were 100 such listings? Life's too short...

There are not, so "what if" would be idle speculation and _that_
would be a waste of my time. <g>

> It isn't the "abuse" of COBOL you should be worrying about, it is the waste
> of your time....

It just so happens that I am retyping the material as I read
it. This gives me more time to absorb the material so that I
may better understand it. And, as a computer program, I can
execute the program and actually see how it did what it did.
I see it as an enhancement of my knowledge. <g>

```
On Jan 2, 6:04 am, Alistair Maclean <alistair.j.l.macl...@gmail.com>
wrote:
> On Jan 2, 2:03 am, Rick Smith <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote:
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> If the language allows it then it can not be abuse.

The language did not allow it. Neither did the language
specifically prohibit it. But it does violate the allowable
content for unsigned numeric display; which for IBM is X"F0"
thru X"F9".

Here is the actual code:
=====
             05  WK-NUMBER             PICTURE 99.
             05  FILLER                REFEFINES WK-NUMBER.
               07  FILLER              PICTURE X.
               07  WK-NUM-UNIT         PICTURE X.
       ...
      1    MOVE ZERO TO WK-NUMBER.
      2    MOVE DWR-TEXT-COL (TX-NEXT) TO WK-NUM-UNIT.
      3    IF X5 IS EQUAL TO 16,
      4        AND WK-NUM-UNIT IS NOT LESS THAN 'A',
      5        AND IS NOT GREATER THAN THAN 'F',
      6        ADD 9 TO WK-NUMBER.
=====
Line 1 places valid values in 'wk-number', i.e., x"F0F0".
Line 2 indirectly moves a potentially invalid character into 'wk-
number',
       specifically a character in the range x"C1" thru x"C6".
Line 6 gives an undefined result.

The undefined result is valid on IBM and can be made valid
elsewhere. However, with the 2002 standard, line 6 will give an
"EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE exception". So, the language now provides
a specific exception condition for what was once undefined.

[snip]

> > > Keying source data from a listing? Why? If the old system can produce a
> > > listing it can produce a file, and if the listing is ALL there is, then I'd
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> listings by hand).

Yes, produced on an IBM 1403N1.
```

```
"Rick Smith" <rs847925@gmail.com> wrote in message 
news:9f158fe4-816b-41aa-af1a-2b04d54bc3a8@o14g2000vbo.googlegroups.com...
On Jan 2, 6:27 am, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> Rick Smith wrote:
> > On Jan 1, 6:37 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
> > <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> >> Rick Smith wrote:
<snip>
It is only the problems with signed versus unsigned numeric display
that appear to conflict with the COBOL standards, both then and now.

.Rick,
   Can you help me understand (you may have already dealt with this) what 
"conflict" there is in gthe handling of signed/unsigned numeric values and 
the Standard (2002 or otherwise).

I am aware that on IBM mainframes, there is a difference in the storage 
between signed positive and unsigned display numeric items while most 
"workstation" (Windows, Linux, etc) do NOT make any distinction between 
these two.  What I don't see is the Standard saying anything about this.

The standard (old and new) only (or mostly only) talks about data items 
where the "data" conforms to the picture.  Therefore, if you have a signed 
item with a sign-nibble of "3", you know it is positive (on those 
environments) if you have an unsigned item with a nibble of "3" then it is 
unsigned.  Nothing in the Standard says that COBOL lets you "determine" if 
the data is signed or unsigned - regardless of the picture clause.
```

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<14aaf0b2-4396-4be1-a8aa-77a1d15cba28@d10g2000vbh.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com> <9mc92bF6n8U1@mid.individual.net> <391fb88f-b320-4fe3-9996-65cf2cf8189a@m7g2000vbc.googlegroups.com> <9mdillFg8U1@mid.individual.net> <9f158fe4-816b-41aa-af1a-2b04d54bc3a8@o14g2000vbo.googlegroups.com> <UuvMq.200684$tf7.4172@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
On Jan 2, 11:29 pm, "Bill Klein" <wmkl...@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
wrote:
> "Rick Smith" <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote in message
>
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> the Standard (2002 or otherwise).

I am not sure how I might have expressed it differently, but it is
the "problems" (i.e., incompatible data) where the conflict arises
-- not in the handling of signed/unsigned data. Prior standards,
to the best of knowledge, treated such "handling" as undefined.
The 2002 standard sets an EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE exception condition.

> I am aware that on IBM mainframes, there is a difference in the storage
> between signed positive and unsigned display numeric items while most
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> the data is signed or unsigned - regardless of the picture clause.

Following is a concise description of the problem.

Given: hex-value pic 99 value 0
and:   move "A" to hex-value (2:1)

On EBCDIC hex-value will contain x"F0C1"
On ASCII  hex-value will contain x"3041"

In both cases the sign nibble conflicts with the picture;
on EBCDIC "C" where "F" is required,
on ASCII  "4" where "3" is required.

IBM ignores the incompatible data: Micro Focus does not.

The other problem, only mentioned here, was actually a COMP-3
item, not display. A table was built of pairs of items:
one pic x(4) the other pic 9(5) comp-3. The pairs were moved
as pic x(7) to a group item, where the corresonding comp-3
was pic s9(5). I removed the 's' to correct the problem.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: "Abuse" of COBOL?

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** "Bill Klein" <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-03T09:47:56-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<PqFMq.189805$Y36.64505@en-nntp-09.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com> <9mc92bF6n8U1@mid.individual.net> <391fb88f-b320-4fe3-9996-65cf2cf8189a@m7g2000vbc.googlegroups.com> <9mdillFg8U1@mid.individual.net> <9f158fe4-816b-41aa-af1a-2b04d54bc3a8@o14g2000vbo.googlegroups.com> <UuvMq.200684$tf7.4172@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com> <14aaf0b2-4396-4be1-a8aa-77a1d15cba28@d10g2000vbh.googlegroups.com>`

```
In both the past and current COBOL standard, "results are undefined" for 
accessing a PIC (( field with incompatible data (except in rare cases). In 
the '02 Standard, it is true that if you have detecting of 
EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE *explicitly* turned on, that then what happens is "well 
defined" but you MUST explicitly turn it on for this to happen.

As far as IBM's handling of PIC 99 fields with (positively) signed data in 
it, there are compiler options that impact how this is handled, e.g. NUMPROC 
and ZWB. (there may be others).

Similarly, I believe that Micro Focus with "-F" run-time in effect, also 
ignores this.

* * * *

Finally, (in general) the idea that COBOL code is "O/S" independent was 
truly a part of the original design (well, originally, it was designed that 
the CONFIGURATION SECTION handled all the "O/S" dependent stuff). However, 
no such claim has been made in decades (by the Standard itself). In the 
early drafts of the '85 Standard, several items were (proposed) to move from 
the File-Control (FD) syntax to the Select/Assign clause. This was 
"rejected" (although it had been this way in the JOD for a while). At that 
time, it was "semi-officially" recognized that there are/were LOTS of O/S 
dependent things in all the sections.


"Rick Smith" <rs847925@gmail.com> wrote in message 
news:14aaf0b2-4396-4be1-a8aa-77a1d15cba28@d10g2000vbh.googlegroups.com...

wrote:
> "Rick Smith" <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote in message
>
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> the Standard (2002 or otherwise).

I am not sure how I might have expressed it differently, but it is
the "problems" (i.e., incompatible data) where the conflict arises
-- not in the handling of signed/unsigned data. Prior standards,
to the best of knowledge, treated such "handling" as undefined.

> between signed positive and unsigned display numeric items while most
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…

- **References:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com> <9mc92bF6n8U1@mid.individual.net> <391fb88f-b320-4fe3-9996-65cf2cf8189a@m7g2000vbc.googlegroups.com> <9mdillFg8U1@mid.individual.net> <9f158fe4-816b-41aa-af1a-2b04d54bc3a8@o14g2000vbo.googlegroups.com> <UuvMq.200684$tf7.4172@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com> <14aaf0b2-4396-4be1-a8aa-77a1d15cba28@d10g2000vbh.googlegroups.com> <PqFMq.189805$Y36.64505@en-nntp-09.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
On Jan 3, 10:47 am, "Bill Klein" <wmkl...@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
wrote:
> In both the past and current COBOL standard, "results are undefined" for
> accessing a PIC (( field with incompatible data (except in rare cases). In
> the '02 Standard, it is true that if you have detecting of
> EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE *explicitly* turned on, that then what happens is "well
> defined" but you MUST explicitly turn it on for this to happen.

The standard is a precise specification for COBOL and there
are two imprecise statements in what you wrote.

-----
ISO/IEC 1989:2002
14.5.12.2 Incompatible data

Incompatible data exists when the content of a sending
operand is not valid only in the following cases:

1) When the content of a boolean or numeric sending
   operand is referenced during the execution of a
   statement and the content of that sending operand
   would evaluate to false in a boolean or numeric
   class condition, respectively, the result of the
   reference is undefined and an EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE
   exception condition is set to exist, except in the
   following circumstances:

   — a sending item is referenced in a class condition, or
   — a sending item is processed in a VALIDATE statement.
-----

First, the result "for accessing a PIC (( field with incompatible
data ..." is defined as "the reference is undefined and an
EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE exception condition is set to exist".
That is, the EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE exception condition occurs
without regard to any TURN directive. And _that_ is consistent
with what I previously stated.

Second, "detecting of EC-DATA-INCOMPATIBLE" need not be explicit.
It may be implicit by using a TURN directive with either EC-ALL
or EC-DATA.


>
> As far as IBM's handling of PIC 99 fields with (positively) signed data in
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> ignores this.

Maybe so; but code that I write never needs it!

>
> * * * *
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> dependent things in all the sections.

So, are you saying the "Common" in "Common Business Oriented
Language" is a lie; mostly false; or mostly true?


>
> "Rick Smith" <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote in message
…[45 more quoted lines elided]…
> IBM ignores the incompatible data: Micro Focus does not.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: "Abuse" of COBOL?

- **References:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com> <9mc92bF6n8U1@mid.individual.net> <391fb88f-b320-4fe3-9996-65cf2cf8189a@m7g2000vbc.googlegroups.com> <9mdillFg8U1@mid.individual.net> <9f158fe4-816b-41aa-af1a-2b04d54bc3a8@o14g2000vbo.googlegroups.com> <UuvMq.200684$tf7.4172@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com> <14aaf0b2-4396-4be1-a8aa-77a1d15cba28@d10g2000vbh.googlegroups.com> <PqFMq.189805$Y36.64505@en-nntp-09.dc1.easynews.com> <d0bbcae2-be6e-4977-a203-ba2c094521ae@j10g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
Rick Smith wrote:
> On Jan 3, 10:47 am, "Bill Klein" <wmkl...@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
> wrote:
<snip>
>> Finally, (in general) the idea that COBOL code is "O/S" independent
>> was truly a part of the original design (well, originally, it was
>> designed that the CONFIGURATION SECTION handled all the "O/S"
>> dependent stuff). However, no such claim has been made in decades
>> (by the Standard itself).

Although I have no great love for the COBOL standard and the pathetic 
mismanagement that engulfed it, I have to completely agree with Bill about 
this.

And it isn't just the standard. For decades, people actually using COBOL 
across different platforms  (and sometimes even on the SAME platform)have 
been forced to the same realization: despite the lofty aspiration that COBOL 
started out with, it failed to achieve proper platform independence.

To be fair, that doesn't make it worthless, because that was only one of the 
opriginal design criteria, and it is also true that nothing else has 
attained it either. The closest thing I can think of would be HTML and 
anyone who has developed web sites knows what a minefield THAT is...

Efforts to produce p-code that could run across platforms have been largely 
doomed to failure. (I remember being very excited by a release of Modula-2 
(since faded into obscurity) which promised this.)

Micro Focus int code  has not been transported to mainframes, for example, 
although, in theory it could be.

Even the .Net CIL (where the "C", like "COBOL", stands for "Common", is 
actually NOT common...)

COBOL was years ahead of its time when it was first discussed and proposed 
and the aspirations of the original CODASYL remain noble to this day. It was 
worth a shot; if it didn't succeed in some areas, that was more than offset 
by benefits provided in other areas.


>> In the early drafts of the '85 Standard,
>> several items were (proposed) to move from the File-Control (FD)
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>

This is Reality biting into dreams, as it usually does... The pragmatists 
cut their losses and move on.

> So, are you saying the "Common" in "Common Business Oriented
> Language" is a lie; mostly false; or mostly true?

That is not a fair question, in my opinion. COBOL is no more "Common" than 
the "Common" cold.  Some people catch one every year, others don't get one 
for a decade or more.

It is true that if you take certain pains to write it a certain way, you 
have a fighting chance of it working on more than one platform, just as, if 
you frequent crowded places in the winter, you are more likely to catch a 
cold...

It seems fair to me that COBOL deserves to retain the word "Common" in its 
name, just as a reminder that it set out to be that and as a tribute to the 
people who wanted it to be that.

But the fact it is called that doesn't make it so.

I am reminded of Abe Lincoln.

"If you call the tail of a horse a "leg", how many legs does the horse 
have?"

(For readers unfamiliar with American folklore, the answer is NOT "5"...)

Pete
```

Rick,
  You are correct that the exception dondition is set, but read on, 
(14.5.12.1 Exception conditions)
"
During the execution of any statement, if checking for an exception 
condition is not enabled, the exception condition will not be raised, even 
if the events that normally raise the exception condition occur.  Therefore, 
when the general rules for a statement indicate that a specific exception 
condition exists, it is raised only if checking for that exception condition 
is enabled."

This means that the run-time behavior (for incompatible data) is EXACTLY the 
same in the '85 and '02 Standards *unless* an explicit) TURN directive is 
used to turn on such checking. (You are correct, it may be a level 3, 
level-2, or level 1 TURN directive). For upward compatility, ALL exception 
checking is set to OFF by default.

```
On Jan 6, 1:02 am, "Bill Klein" <wmkl...@noreply.ix.netcom.com> wrote:
> Rick,
>   You are correct that the exception dondition is set, but read on,
> (14.5.12.1 Exception conditions)

[snip]

> This means that the run-time behavior (for incompatible data) is EXACTLY the
> same in the '85 and '02 Standards *unless* an explicit) TURN directive is
> used to turn on such checking. (You are correct, it may be a level 3,
> level-2, or level 1 TURN directive). For upward compatility, ALL exception
> checking is set to OFF by default.

The standard doesn't provide any assurance that "run-time
behavior (for incompatible data) is EXACTLY the same".
-----
ISO/IEC 1989:2002
3.3 A conforming run unit
...
Situations in which the results of executing a statement
are explicitly undefined or unpredictable are identified
in B.2, Undefined language element list. A COBOL run unit
that allows these situations to happen is a conforming
run unit, although the resultant execution is not defined
by standard COBOL.
-----
The most that one may say is "in the '85 and [, specifically,]
'02 Standards" "the resultant execution is not defined by
standard COBOL."

Now, it is NOT likely that behavior, for incompatible data,
will change; but, if it does, it is not due to the standard,
nor conformance thereto. Rather, it is the result of
"allow[ing] these situations to happen".
```

I'm not sure what compilers would or wouldn't support the following, 
neither am I sure what the Very Good Reason is for delving into hexvals in 
a language intended for Common, Business-Oriented Programming... but for 
something quick and dirty:

 01  ws-codeset-test pic x value low-values.
     88  ascii-environment  value x'20'.
     88  ebcdic-environment value x'40.

...

 move space to ws-codeset-test
 evaluate true
     when ascii-environment
         PERFORM A12755-TWIDDLE-BITS  THRU  A12755-EXIT
     when ebcdic-environment
         PERFORM A12756-BITS-TWIDDLE  THRU  A12756-EXIT
     when other
***code should never, ever get here
         DISPLAY ' CODE SHOULD NEVER, EVER GET HERE '
         DISPLAY ' CONTACT PROGRAMMING '
         DISPLAY ' ABENDING RUN '
         MOVE WS-ABEND-CODE-UNKNOWN  TO  WS-ABENDING-CODE
         GO TO 9999-ALLES-GEHT-KERFLOOIE
 end-evaluate

>
>I added the following similar code before line 21.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>                   to hex-value (2:1)

I don't think I'd like to see that at 2:am with the batch window 
closing... but I am simple-minded, that way.

[snip]

>The question then is: What are 'good', platform-independent
>ways for converting hexadecimal characters to numeric values?

Perhaps the same ways that keep track of the codepage being used during 
the runtime.

It might make one wonder if anyone - yourself included - would be able to 
determine if what you'd asked has been answered.

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: "Abuse" of COBOL?

- **From:** Robert Wessel <robertwessel2@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-02T06:34:58-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8763g7phqveum11hduiaepd5svk1n4qmub@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Sun, 1 Jan 2012 09:13:44 -0800 (PST), Rick Smith
<rs847925@gmail.com> wrote:

>The following program demonstrates a problem I encountered while
>converting old IBM code to ANSI 85 for a computer that uses ASCII.
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
>=====


Frankly, I'm having trouble seeing how you could expect that to work
on any platform.  If you have a value greater than 9, the (display
numeric) hex-value will not be a valid number (IOW, it should fail "IS
NUMERIC" as this is an unsigned field and an overpunch style sign
wouldn't be allowed), and adding 9 to it isn't going work, except by
some quirk of the code generated to do the arithmetic.

On an IBM mainframe, this would work because of the way the character
ser is laid out, how the pack instruction works, the fact that C is a
valid positive sign, and the typical generated code (PACK/AP/UNPK/OI),
but I fail to see anything that would guarantee the result.


>Now, assuming that 'hex-value' (line 8) must be maintained
>as is, what remediation is required to use ASCII characters?
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
>ways for converting hexadecimal characters to numeric values?


All of the platform independent ways I can think of are pretty clumsy.
If you were willing to assume that 0-9 and A-F are each contiguous in
the character set (true in EBCDIC and ASCII, but not required by the
standard), something like this is reasonable, but I'd code it as:

  if hex-char < "0" or hex-char > "9" then
    hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - function ord("A") + 10
  else
    hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - function ord("0")
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: "Abuse" of COBOL?

- **From:** Rick Smith <rs847925@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-02T12:11:00-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b80ea2b1-097f-48b3-9ccf-8d3fc699a6de@m10g2000vbc.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<d9e62d87-d561-4fa1-a2e0-0121f328aa0a@t16g2000vba.googlegroups.com> <8763g7phqveum11hduiaepd5svk1n4qmub@4ax.com>`

```
On Jan 2, 7:34 am, Robert Wessel <robertwess...@yahoo.com> wrote:
> On Sun, 1 Jan 2012 09:13:44 -0800 (PST), Rick Smith
> <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote:


[snip]

> >=====
> >      $set charset "ebcdic" badsigns apost

[snip]

> Frankly, I'm having trouble seeing how you could expect that to work
> on any platform.  If you have a value greater than 9, the (display
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> but I fail to see anything that would guarantee the result.

I was working on my response to Alistair before reading your
post and most of what you say is addressed there; but, basically,
if at any time a numeric field would not pass an IS NUMERIC class
test it would be invalid to use that field except as a receiving
field.

[snip]

> >The question then is: What are 'good', platform-independent
> >ways for converting hexadecimal characters to numeric values?
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>     hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - function ord("0")
    end-if

The condition might seem a bit unclear to some.

    evaluate hex-char
    when "0" thru "9"
        hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - function ord("0")
    when "A" thru "F"
        hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - function ord("A") + 10
    when "a" thru "f"
        hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - function ord("a") + 10
    when other
* insert error code here
        continue
    end-evaluate

Covers all the bases, so to speak.

I am not sure what you may see a "pretty clumsy"; but,
another way is a subprogram using 'function ord ()':
=====
       identification division.
       program-id. hex-sub.
       environment division.
       configuration section.
       object-computer. cobol-85
           sequence hexadecimal-alphabet.
       special-names.
           alphabet hexadecimal-alphabet "0" thru "9"
               "A" also "a" "B" also "b" "C" also "c"
               "D" also "d" "E" also "e" "F" also "f".
       data division.
       linkage section.
       01  hex-char pic x.
       01  hex-value pic 99.
       procedure division using hex-char hex-value.
       begin.
           compute hex-value = function ord (hex-char) - 1
           exit program
           .
=====
(This program cannot be a nested program.)

Other platform-independent ways may use loops to scan a list
of valid hexadecimal characters to determine the relative value,
none of which seem clumsy to me.
```

<a id="t-d899a8da54"></a>
## Thread: .so file — 3 msgs

### .so file

- **From:** Alain Reymond <arwebmail@skynet.be>
- **Date:** 2012-01-02T16:46:27+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4f01d16a$0$5053$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`

```
Hello,

Here is a little problem :

Let's say I have a c file cprog.c with :
---- begin cprog.c
cfunc1  (st, c)
char  *st;
int   *c;
{
        ....
        return(0);
}

cfunc2  (st, c)
char  *st;
int   *c;
{
        ....
        return(0);
}
---- end cprog.c

How to create an .so from the c file under unix to be able to call the
functions from a Cobol file under Micro Focus cobol :

---- cblprog.cbl ----
working-storage section.
01 str.
          03 str-text    pic x(10).
          03 filler      pic x  value x"00".   *>Null terminate string
for C function
01 counter  pic 9(8) comp-5  value zero.

procedure division.
         call "cfunc1" using str, counter
         call "cfunc2" using str, counter
         if return-code not = zero
              display "ERROR"
          else
              display "OK"
          end-if
         stop run.


Best regards and happy new year!

Alain
```

#### ↳ Re: .so file

- **From:** Brian Tiffin <bwtiffin@yahoo.ca>
- **Date:** 2012-01-02T12:56:25-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3f2e8c1a-3b7c-48b5-9b0f-d5e42d92abe2@t30g2000vbx.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4f01d16a$0$5053$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`

```
On Jan 2, 10:46 am, Alain Reymond <arwebm...@skynet.be> wrote:
> Hello,
>
…[45 more quoted lines elided]…
> Alain

OpenCOBOL with Fedora GNU/Linux generates the small library of

----errn.c-----

#include <errno.h>

int get_errno() {
    return errno;
}

int set_errno(int en) {
    int oen;
    oen = errno;
    errno = en;
    return oen;
}
--------

using

----terminal session----
[btiffin@home cobol]$ cobc -v -m errn.c
Command line:   cobc -v -m errn.c
Executing:      gcc -std=gnu99 -I/usr/local/include -pipe -Wno-unused
                -fsigned-char -fno-gcse -Wno-pointer-sign -fomit-frame-
pointer
                -fno-asynchronous-unwind-tables -U_FORTIFY_SOURCE -
shared
                -fPIC -DPIC -Wl,--export-dynamic -o "errn.so" "errn.c"
                -L/usr/local/lib -lcob -lm -lgmp -lncursesw -ldb -ldl
Return status:  0
--------

The critical bits being -fPIC, -DPIC, -shared which influence the link
phase.  PIC for Position Independent Code (and -D defined so the
assembler phase can be smart about the PIC as well). -shared to inform
the toolchain that shared object output is expected. --export-dynamic
informs the linker to include all symbols which can make using dlopen
more featureful.

The output of the above is errn.so that can be linked to by anything
that plays nice with the C application binary interface.

On *nix system not running gcc, have a look to the man pages for the
local cc, then ar and ranlib.  If you do have gcc, you might have GNU
autotools in which case you want to look into libtool.  libtool is
crafted for each supported platform to make static, shared and
convenience archives, umm, conveniently.

Or, get OpenCOBOL on the target platform and use its handy compiler
options to generate dynamic shared objects with relative ease.  In the
above, I just has to use  cobc with -v (to get verbose output of the
commands used in the toolchain) and -m for create a module please.
cobc does the right thing when asked to compile .c files, and does the
right thing on the platform for -x executables, -m modules and even -b
which combines all input files into a single module.

Cheers,
Brian
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: .so file

- **From:** Alain Reymond <arwebmail@skynet.be>
- **Date:** 2012-01-03T16:22:29+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4f031d51$0$5038$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<3f2e8c1a-3b7c-48b5-9b0f-d5e42d92abe2@t30g2000vbx.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4f01d16a$0$5053$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be> <3f2e8c1a-3b7c-48b5-9b0f-d5e42d92abe2@t30g2000vbx.googlegroups.com>`

```
Le 02/01/2012 21:56, Brian Tiffin a ï¿½crit :
> On Jan 2, 10:46 am, Alain Reymond <arwebm...@skynet.be> wrote:
>> Hello,
…[105 more quoted lines elided]…
> Brian

Thank you for this complete information.

Under MF Cobol, I can create a .so file for the cprog.c file :
cob -Z cprog.c -o cprog.so

And then compile and link the cbl file with the .so :
cob -x cobprog.cbl cprog.so

If I still want to use ing org gnt files, I can create a new runtime
linked to the so file :
cob -xo rtsnew cprog.so

compile the cobol program :
cob cobprog.cbl
and then use :
./rtsnew cobprog

Regards

Alain
```

## Thread: OT: Career advice — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Jobs, careers, recruiting, salary`](topics.md#jobs) · [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT: Career advice

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-04T02:22:19+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9mgdodF9lcU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
I came across the following as part of a much larger article and thought it 
might amuse some here.

My personal favourite is point 4, but I can relate to nearly all of them...

Enjoy!

SIGNS THAT YOU SHOULDN'T BE A PROGRAMMER:

(The following may not have any remedies if you still suffer from them after 
taking a programming course in school, so you will stand a better chance of 
advancing your career by choosing another profession.)

1. Inability to determine the order of program execution
Symptoms:

a = 5
b = 10
a = b
print a

You look at the code above and aren't sure what number gets printed out at 
the end

Alternative careers:
Electrician
Plumber
Architect
Civil engineer

2. Insufficient ability to think abstractly
Symptoms:

Difficulty comprehending the difference between objects and classes
Difficulty implementing design patterns for your program
Difficulty writing functions with low cohesion
Incompetence with Regular Expressions
Lisp is opaque to you
Cannot fathom the Church-Turing Thesis

Alternative careers:

Contract negotiator
Method actor

3. Collyer Brothers syndrome
Symptoms:

Unwilling to throw away anything, including garbage
Unwilling to delete anything, be it code or comments
The urge to build booby-traps for defense against trespassers
Unwilling to communicate with other people
Poor organization skills

Alternative careers:

Antique dealer
Bag lady

4. Dysfunctional sense of causality
Symptoms:

You seriously consider malice to be a reason why the compiler rejects your 
program
When called on to fix a bug in a deployed program, you try prayer
You take hidden variables for granted and don't think twice about blaming 
them for a program's misbehavior
You think the presence of code in a program will affect its runtime 
behavior, even if it is never invoked
Your debugging repertoire includes rituals like shining your lucky golf 
ball, twisting your wedding ring, and tapping the nodding-dog toy on your 
monitor. And when the debugging doesn't work, you think it might be because 
you missed one or didn't do them in the right order

Alternative careers:

Playing the slot machines in Vegas

5. Indifference to outcomes
Programming could still be a hobby for you, but it would be in society's 
best interests to defend itself against your entry into the world of 
professional software development.
Symptoms:

You aren't interested in fixing a bug that can be worked around by rebooting 
the computer
Your installation program silently deploys unsolicited third party programs 
that are unrelated to the function of yours *
You don't use any ergonomic model when designing user interfaces, nor do you 
have any interest in usability studies
Your program exhibits pretension and grandeur beyond its utility, eg: 
displaying splash screens over active programs while loading in the 
background, or placing multiple launch icons in premium desktop locations *
Your program produces output to be read by another (eg: a browser), or 
implements a network protocol, and relies on the other party's software to 
be significantly tolerant to spec violations
You write busy-wait loops even when the platform offers event-driven 
programming
You don't use managed languages and can't be bothered to do bounds checking 
or input validation
Your user interfaces do not make the difficulty of accidentally invoking a 
function proportionate to its destructiveness (eg: the "Delete Database" 
button is next to "Save", just as big, has no confirmation step and no undo)
You don't use whitespace, indentation or comments
* - These are actually imposed by management more often than by the 
programmer, who only implements them. We'd still group them together for the 
sake of this self-test, though, and at the most suggest that one seek 
employment at a better firm, while the other goes back to business school to 
learn less destructive ways of making a profit.

Alternative careers:

Debt collection
Telemarketing

All contents are Public Domain

Pete.
```

Pete Dashwood <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
>HeyBub wrote:
>> ... in a TV ad? I'll tell you: all hell breaks loose!
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
>Minister... pull some strings."

I'm not sure how these things work in the Antipodes, Mr Dashwood, but here 
in the United States of America the balancing of Freedom of Speech with 
various other Rights, laws, rules, regulations and social changes seems 
still to be a Work in Progress.

From 
<http://groups.google.com/group/comp.lang.cobol/msg/620a55a923330957?hl=en&dmode=source>

--begin quoted text:

'I am not an advocate for frequent changes in laws and constitutions, but 
laws and institutions must go hand in hand with the progress of the human 
mind. As that becomes more developed, more enlightened, as new discoveries 
are made, new truths discovered and manners and opinions change, with the 
change of circumstances, institutions must advance also to keep pace with 
the times. We might as well require a man to wear still the coat which 
fitted him when a boy as civilized society to remain ever under the 
regimen of their barbarous ancestors.'

These words of Jefferson are written in the stones of his Memorial, Mr 
Summers.  'Laws and instutituions' must keep pace with 'manners and 
opinions'; to ask for otherwise is to request a kind of stagnance which 
appears, to the above-stated sentiments, to be utterly repugnant.

--end quoted text

DD

alternative to MS , and working side by side with Linux , kept the Web
alive , growing and well , thank you Steve Jobs !!!

creative , smart and free Web , and that's why the news from the new

<a id="t-ccf5f1a7cd"></a>
## Thread: OT: The yearning for learning... — 16 msgs

_Topics: [`Tutorials, books, learning`](topics.md#learning) · [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT: The yearning for learning...

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-06T14:10:23+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9mn000FarjU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Those nice people at Microsoft have recently released a complete series of 
videos (24 of them) aimed at absolute beginners (although I went through a 
number of them myself and it did me no harm...), that explain step by step 
the concepts and details of programming in C# and using the Visual Studio 
IDE.

It's a new year. Maybe time to invest in some learning?

You couldn't get a better tutor than Bob Tabor and most of what I know about 
C# I learned from him. (I also took his advice and used other resources to 
expand and consolidate the fundamental concepts he teaches.) So far, in 
cash, I have spent around $35 for some second hand books on C#. The code I 
have written with it has generated considerably more than that :-) so my 
time (and money) was well spent.

People interested in developing for .Net (and other things in the future) 
using FREE software, no runtime licensing, and now with FREE tuition, should 
invest just under 5 minutes of their busy lives and check out:

http://channel9.msdn.com/Series/C-Sharp-Fundamentals-Development-for-Absolute-Beginners

Although learning stuff is not JUST about money, you are unlikley to get a 
better return on your investment than this.

The skills you can acquire here don't just look good on a CV, they are a 
positive asset to your personal growth experience. For myself, I found that 
setting aside what I already knew and approaching the subject as if I knew 
nothing, provided some very interesting insights into things I DID already 
know. (Although you can set what you know aside, you certainly don't forget 
it completely :-) Just don't evaluate the new information through a filter 
of the old.)

Instead of trying to measure new information against old information, 
measure it against nothing. Just spend some time and get your head around 
it. When you do this, you will see the old information in a series of new 
lights and the total experience is now broader and better. (In effect, 
learning new stuff can actually improve your perception of the old stuff, 
even if you are quite sure you have nothing to learn about it. (Learning 
Java and C# made me a better COBOL programmer...It also extended my 
"programming power" so I could tackle much more complex problems than I had 
previously...)

I know that most of you will let this opportunity slip away :-) but my 
conscience would have bothered me if I didn't at least give you an option 
:-)

Pete.

PS If anyone does actually do this course (and you can do it at your own 
pace in your own time) please let me know what you thought about it. I'm 
curious to see whether my own very positive experience is a general one.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OT: The yearning for learning...

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-12T23:28:37+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9n7qumF2ggU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<9mn000FarjU1@mid.individual.net> <sh9eg79o0tgh18n047l00m9lusjv5uc84a@4ax.com> <9mphi3F27cU1@mid.individual.net> <jkbrg7ll1hlv6d1rn45p48sit7epdcar7g@4ax.com>`

```
SkippyPB wrote:
> On Sat, 7 Jan 2012 13:22:25 +1300, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[83 more quoted lines elided]…
> to write once I get enough basic knowledge to attempt it.

Don't jump your hurdles 'til you come to them... :-)

Using C# code-behinds in ASP.Net is slightly different from using C# on the 
desktop, but fortunately, VS knows the difference and does most of it for 
you. Instead of setting up a Windows project or a console project (no GUI), 
you select a Web Project and VS puts all the infrastructure in place for 
you. It is pretty cool really.

The IDE makes a HUGE difference to the power of the tools. Most of the 
"benefits" claimed for Micro Focus Visual COBOL are provided by VS 2010 and 
are available to any language that uses it.

BTW, I have been using Net Express 5.1 recently and I have decided that the 
MF IDE is absolutely the WORST I have ever encountered, anywhere. I can 
understand why they were all so keen to move to VS 2010. :-)



>
> I'll post follow up status info just as an FYI for anyone else that is
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
It is only "weird" because you're not used to it :-)

Yes, I had trouble with that when I first started (and I couldn't understand 
what the Hell a "namespace" was or why you would need one :-))

The best thing with the braces (at least it works for me...) is to interpret 
"{" mentally as "start block", and "}" as "end block", then it kind of falls 
into place.

Also, I found fairly soon in the piece that I liked to have the braces NOT 
indented... so:

if (some condition)
{ <= "start block"
    do lots of stuff
} <= "end block

... rather than:

if (some condition)
    {
        do lots of stuff
}

...or...

if (some condition)
    {
        do lots of stuff
    }

Fortunately VS is clever enough to pick up your preferences and after I 
adjusted the braces a few times, it started placing them where I wanted 
them.

The use of braces and namespaces does become apparent after a little while 
and these days I don't think twice about them.

Just one tip...

C# allows you to make a single statement without it being in a block, but 
you CAN put it in a block if you want. This is a bit confusing because you 
may see things like:

if (some condition)
    do something...
else
{
    do lots of stuff
}

Although that is perfectly valid, so is this:

if (some condition)
{
    do something...
}
else
{
    do lots of stuff
}


The thing to remember is that if you have more than one statement in an 
action, it MUST be a block, otherwise it MAY be a block.

Like everything, once you're used to it, it seems perfectly natural.

Also, If you select a brace with the cursor, VS will grey the corresponding 
brace so you can check they match and the block(s) are consistent.

HTH,

Pete.
```

```
SkippyPB wrote:
> On Thu, 12 Jan 2012 23:28:37 +1300, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
>
<snip>>
> Thanks for the tips.  I've noticed that indenting behavior.  And of
> course now I also have to remember to use () for methods and [] for
> arrays as well.

This is actually a Good Thing. Method signatures need parentheses and you 
will have seen how Intellisense gives you clues as soon as you open them 
when you are referencing an already defined method.

The brackets make sure there is no confusion between array elements and 
method signatures. (if they weren't there and you encountered:

accountBalance(11)

... you wouldn't know whether it was a method being passed a numeric 
parameter, or a bunch of balances referencing the 11th one.)

It might just be me, but I tend not to use arrays a lot, preferring various 
types of collection (which come with ready made Methods I don't have to 
write) instead. It is different from COBOL where the collections available 
are a bit limited and you still have to do quite a bit of work to use them.
I especially like the "stack" collection which automatically provides POP 
and PUSH methods. I thought I would have to write it myself but Intellisense 
told me I didn't. And it worked correctly straight out of the box... always 
surprising with things IT :-)

The way collections are implemented you usually get the best of both worlds; 
you can reference your collection using a key or an index in parentheses as 
a collection method, but you can also reference it as an array (by using a 
bracket).

Don't worry. Like most things as you practice it, it becomes more familiar 
and clearer.

>
> The IDE is nice albiet very slow on my PC until it gets going.

Google is your friend. I seem to remember a number of pages offering advice 
to speed up VS. Beware of shonky registry cleaners, but amongst the dross 
there is some sensible advice for configuring VS.

Pete.
```

```
HeyBub wrote:
> Alistair Maclean wrote:
>> On Jan 13, 3:04 am, "Pete Dashwood"
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
> library shelf or alphabetizing items in the pantry.

Not sure I totally agree with that, although you can certainly survive 
without a Registry cleaner...

The times when I find it useful are as follows:

1. I have been messing with the Registry and need to remove everything I 
did.  (A good registry cleaner matches registry entries against files in the 
system and removes the entry (actually, flags it for removal and notifies 
you) if it is in a place where it should refer to a file but no such file 
exists.)

2. The Registry has become highly fragmented due to high volatility and is 
consequently degrading overall system performance. (Defragmenting the 
registry when it actually needs it can show a marked improvement in 
performance. A good registry cleaner will also offer a registry 
defragmentation service.)

3. I have been adding and deleting COM servers and registering  and 
de-registering them and now I want a clean slate for the "final copy". 
(Rename the .DLL, unregister it with regsvr32, then run a registry clean 
before renaming it back to what it should be and registering it again with 
regsvr32)

If I ran a registry clean more than 3 times a year I'd start looking at why 
I needed to...

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OT: The yearning for learning...

_(thread depth: 11)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-16T00:06:30+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9nfq9oF9cbU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<9mn000FarjU1@mid.individual.net> <sh9eg79o0tgh18n047l00m9lusjv5uc84a@4ax.com> <9mphi3F27cU1@mid.individual.net> <jkbrg7ll1hlv6d1rn45p48sit7epdcar7g@4ax.com> <9n7qumF2ggU1@mid.individual.net> <a7vtg7hinbihqcq585qftbng4mv73fkusj@4ax.com> <9n9labFu9sU1@mid.individual.net> <4dfacf4d-e641-4c52-a4e7-7a49dd55887a@do4g2000vbb.googlegroups.com> <Q6-dnZNFQpHsEIzSnZ2dnUVZ_uWdnZ2d@earthlink.com> <9neeenF69uU1@mid.individual.net> <0tednWhygN4QzI_SnZ2dnUVZ_gKdnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
HeyBub wrote:
> Pete Dashwood wrote:
>>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> definition, cannot be "fragmented."

Are you saying a "database" cannot become fragmented?

Every RDBMS I have ever worked with goes to great pains to deal with 
fragmentation under the covers. Even balanced trees like Btrieve and VSAM 
which split storage areas to create free space automatically and avoid 
second level overflow on indexed datasets, still can become fragmented and 
need reloading occasionally. Access, SQL Server, Oracle, DB2, SQL Lite, 
MySQL and PostgreSQL ALL can experience "fragmentation", inasmuch as DB 
pages can become split and "misplaced". Most RDBMS implement "clustering" to 
overcome this but usually it is up to the DBA to decide what needs 
clustering and what doesn't. To be fair, is it usually well handled 
transparently but eventually a DB will need to be reloaded in order to 
improve performance.Talk to anyone who has worked as a DBA for a few years.

If you think the Windows registry is "a highly-optimized relational database 
" you have either been severely misinformed or you have never worked with 
physical Registry hives (I have...)

The Registry hives are five physical binary files with a particular 
structure (Page>Block>Cell/Bin) which are manipulated in memory almost as if 
they were system pages. Most of what you see in the Registry is created in 
memory at run time by the Configuration Manager element of the Windows 
kernel stitiching together various base keys held in the hives. It is not 
physically anything like the structure you see and it is not physically like 
a relational database either. It is a hierarchic key system and there are no 
relational constraints OTHER than Hierarchy implemented by it.

> It CAN have unused space or
> entries, but whether it has 1000 entries or 100,000 has no detectable
> effect on the efficiency of the overall system.

"Nope.", Huh? :-)

Having had a bit of experience with "highly optimized relational databases" 
over the last 30 years, since they were invented, (I have worked with all of 
the ones mentioned above plus a couple of others) I can assure you Registry 
hives and page files CAN become fragmented. Frequent insertion will cause it 
even though free space is automatically created as insertions occur. There 
are also times when the Registry needs to be searched. If Registry hive 
blocks get split across physical 4K pages or linked keys are in different 
blocks as a result of bin (free space) allocation, it can and does seriously 
degrade overall system performance.

But don't take my word for it...

Mark Russinovich is an acknowledged authority on Microsoft system internals 
and Technical Fellow at Microsoft (I use a number of his usually free system 
utilities).

Here's what HE said  on 10th July, 2005 on being asked if a bloated Registry 
could seriously degrade performance::

"No, even if the registry was massively bloated there would be little impact 
on the performance of anything other than exhaustive searches.

On Win2K Terminal Server systems, however, there is a limit on the total 
amount of Registry data that can be loaded and so large profile hives can 
limit the number of users that can be logged on simultaneously.

I haven't and never will implement a Registry cleaner since it's of little 
practical use on anything other than Win2K terminal servers and developing 
one that's both safe and effective requires a huge amount of 
application-specific knowledge."

He then spent some time investigating, thinking about it, and writing a 
registry defrag tool. In November 2006 he said:

"One of the limitations of the Windows NT/2000 defragmentation interface is 
that it is not possible to defragment files that are open for exclusive 
access. Thus, standard defragmentation programs can neither show you how 
fragmented your paging files or Registry hives are, nor defragment them.

Paging and Registry file fragmentation can be one of the leading causes of 
performance degradation related to file fragmentation in a system."

Please note the last sentence.

If neither Mark nor myself have any credibility with you, perhaps a word 
from those nice people at Microsoft...

"Processes that use the registry to repeatedly modify the same values in 
small increments can cause excessive memory fragmentation in the 
corresponding registry hive. The sum of the fragmented cells can become so 
large that the hive size winds up many times larger than the sum of actual 
data in the hive. Eventually, the sum of the hive will exceed the Registry 
Size Limit (RSL), causing subsequent modifications to fail until the RSL is 
increased. As an example consider the SAM hive used to store Windows NT 
accounts. The SAM size frequently exceeds projected sizes due to the fact 
that it fragments the SAM hive when adding members to large groups. "

You can get the full story on this aspect of it (and it is only one aspect, 
that doesn't apply to all versions of the Windows OS), from:

http://support.microsoft.com/kb/197632

Still not convinced? I searched MSDN with Bing and found 111000 entries 
discussing registry fragmentation...(Not all are pertinent to this 
discussion. :-))

In the final analysis empirical data and results trump theory every time. 
(If they disagree, it is the theory that has to be modified.)

I KNOW that performance on my system improves if I defrag the Registry 
Hives, PROVIDED they actually NEED defragging. Programs load faster, COM 
components activate more quickly, and the general impression is one of 
improvement.

Next time you say "Nope" to a post from me, maybe check exactly what it is 
you're saying "No" to?

I don't claim infallibility (leave that to the Pope) but I do post based on 
actual experience.

Pete.
```

## Thread: eScan Anti-Virus for Linux Desktop — 1 msgs

### eScan Anti-Virus for Linux Desktop

- **From:** Web Master <wmaster711@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-01-05T23:49:47-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e73de303-9eb6-4deb-9368-8e863925e3c5@t13g2000yqg.googlegroups.com>`

```
eScan Anti-Virus for Linux Desktops (eScan) is a reliable virus
scanning software for machines running on Linux, which protects your
machines from virus and other threats, thus offering you a complete

## Thread: Cobol-C problems — 8 msgs

### Cobol-C problems

- **From:** Alain Reymond <arwebmail@skynet.be>
- **Date:** 2012-01-06T14:16:50+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4f06f44a$0$5034$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`

```
Hello,

I have problems using a C library under RHEL5, serverexpress 5.
I installed the libharu library to be able to create pdf files. Very
easy : from the http://libharu.org/wiki/Downloads I downloaded the last
stable version, then configure, make, make install and the library is
installed. I checked with C examples from the libharu site : a simple
compile using
|gcc font_demo.c -l hpdf|
does the job and the program generates the pdf file.

I used h2cpy to generate properly the types according to libharu .h
files. In fact, most of the functions work with pointers (maybe, that's
my problem).
I created a small cobol sample program which is the translation of a C
demo file font_demo.cbl.
No problem at compliation time using :
|cob -x font_demo.cbl -l hpdf|
It even runs without problem, except that the final results are
completly wrong!! At the beginning of the program, it asks for the size
of the page which should be (841, 595) and I find negative values... And
the file is not generated...

I suspect that the problem resides in the pointer use. But I can't find
the origin of the problem.
If there are any suggestions...

Best regards and thanks.

|
       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID. 'fontdemo'.
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.
       FILE-CONTROL.
       DATA DIVISION.
       FILE SECTION.
      $set sourceformat"free"
       working-storage section.
       *>copy "ctypes.cpy".
       copy "hpdf_types.cpy".
       1 HPDF-Doc          is typedef       usage pointer.
       1 HPDF-Font         is typedef       usage pointer.
       1 HPDF-Page         is typedef       usage pointer.

       1 page-title  pic x(50) value z"Font Demo".
       1 fname       pic x(256).
       1 def-font    usage HPDF-Font.
       1 tw          usage HPDF-REAL.
       1 myheight    usage HPDF-REAL.
       1 mywidth     usage HPDF-REAL.
       1 myheight1   usage HPDF-REAL.
       1 mywidth1    usage HPDF-REAL.
       1 i           usage HPDF-UINT.
       1 mypage      usage HPDF-Page.
       1 pdf         usage HPDF-Doc.
       1 pdfstatus   usage HPDF-STATUS.
       
       1 aa          pic +99999.9999.
       1 txt         pic x(256).
       
      $set sourceformat"free"
       procedure division.

         call "HPDF_New" using NULL, NULL returning pdf
         display "HPDF_New " pdf
         if (pdf = NULL) then
            display "error: cannot create PdfDoc object"
            exit program
         end-if
         *>HPDF_STATUS HPDF_GetError (HPDF_Doc pdf);
         call "HPDF_GetError" using by value pdf returning pdfstatus
         display "status " pdfstatus         

         *> Add a new page object. */
         *>page = HPDF_AddPage (pdf);
         call "HPDF_AddPage" using by value pdf returning mypage

         *> Should be height : 841.000000  width : 595.000000
         *>myheight = HPDF_Page_GetHeight (mypage);
         call "HPDF_Page_GetHeight" using by value mypage returning myheight
         *>mywidth = HPDF_Page_GetWidth (mypage);
         call "HPDF_Page_GetWidth" using by value mypage returning mywidth

         *> Print the lines of the page. */
         *>HPDF_Page_SetLineWidth (mypage, 1);
         call "HPDF_Page_SetLineWidth" using by value mypage, 1
         *>HPDF_Page_Rectangle (mypage, 50, 50, mywidth - 100, myheight
- 110);
         compute mywidth1 = mywidth - 100
         compute myheight1 = myheight - 110
         call "HPDF_Page_Rectangle" using by value mypage, 50, 50,
mywidth1, myheight1
         *>HPDF_Page_Stroke (mypage);
         call "HPDF_Page_Stroke" using mypage

         *> output subtitle. */
         *>HPDF_Page_BeginText (mypage);
         call "HPDF_Page_BeginText" using by value mypage
         *>HPDF_Page_SetFontAndSize (mypage, def_font, 16);
         *>HPDF_Page_TextOut (mypage, 60, myheight - 80, "<Standerd
Type1 fonts samples>");
         compute myheight1 = myheight - 80
         move z"<Standerd Type1 fonts samples>" to txt
         call "HPDF_Page_TextOut" using by value mypage, 60, myheight1,
by reference txt
         *>HPDF_Page_EndText (mypage);
         call "HPDF_Page_EndText" using by value mypage         

         *>HPDF_SaveToFile (pdf, fname);
         move z'cblfontdemo.pdf' to fname
         call "HPDF_SaveToFile" using by value pdf, by reference fname

         *> clean up */
         *>HPDF_Free (pdf);
         call "HPDF_Free" using by value pdf

         exit program
         stop run
         .

|

#### ↳ Re: Cobol-C problems

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-07T13:52:07+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9mpjq4FgurU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4f06f44a$0$5034$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`

```
Alain Reymond wrote:
> Hello,
>
…[120 more quoted lines elided]…
>         .

Alain,

I'm not familiar with the library you are using but the thought strikes me 
that instead of using C type typedefs it might be better to use object 
references. Can you instantiate the library and then invoke the methods as 
methods of an object?

The other thing I noticed is some confusion over "by value" and "by 
reference"... if you specify one of these it remains in effect until you 
specify the other, and the default is "by reference", for COBOL. So, try 
changing...

call "HPDF_Page_Rectangle" using by value mypage, 50, 50,
mywidth1, myheight1

..to be..

call "HPDF_Page_Rectangle"
      using
             by value
                  mypage, 50, 50
             by reference
                  mywidth1, myheight1
       ON EXCEPTION
              ...whatever...
end-call

You might need to address this in other places as well; I haven't fine 
combed the code you posted.

Let us know what happens :-)

Pete.
```

To complete my previous message, I found some curious problems. To be

file like :

HPDF_Font CBL_HPDF_GetFont (HPDF_Doc pdf, const char *font_name, const
char  *encoding_name){
      HPDF_Font font;   
      font = HPDF_GetFont(pdf, font_name, encoding_name);
      return font;
}

float CBL_HPDF_Page_GetWidth (HPDF_Page hPage) {
      float fXPos;
      fXPos = HPDF_Page_GetWidth(hPage);
      return fXPos;  
}
etc...
So the CBL program does not call the libharu C function, but calls a C
function that calls the libharu library. A kind of wrapper. I could then
fix a curious problem using float : the page width and height was never
correct when I called the libharu HPDF_Page_GetWidth from Cobol, but
correct when called through my "wrapper". Obviously a problem of type
defintion.

More curious, from Cobol, the HPDF_Page_TextOut gives an error in the
pdf file. But when I call successively HPDF_Page_MoveTextPos and
HPDF_Page_ShowText, the pdf file is correct.
I want to print "titre" at 281.5, 791 as position. If I call
HPDF_Page_TextOut directly, here is the result in the pdf :
stream
/F1 16 Tf
BT
.(-*,( .(-*,( Td
(Titre) Tj
ET

endstream

and the succession of the two functions, here is the result (like in C,
with no compression) :

stream
/F1 16 Tf
BT
281.5 791 Td
(Titre) Tj
ET

endstr

I use Micro Focus serverexpress under Linux Centos5. But I also tried

the variable definitions, can't give the same results...

Alain Reymond wrote:

And, presumably, it is still wrong? :-)
>
> To complete my previous message, I found some curious problems. To be
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
> function that calls the libharu library. A kind of wrapper.

Good idea...

> I could
> then fix a curious problem using float : the page width and height
> was never correct when I called the libharu HPDF_Page_GetWidth from
> Cobol, but correct when called through my "wrapper". Obviously a
> problem of type defintion.

Or pointer addressing. That was why I suggested using By Reference for the 
calculated fields.

Good that you got it working, though.


>
> More curious, from Cobol, the HPDF_Page_TextOut gives an error in the
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
> effects.

I have to say, I'd separate the .pdf writing out of the code and simply pass 
a stream to a .pdf engine. But, given you have the library, I guess it is 
understandable you want to use it :-)
>
> I can't figure why a small program translated exactly the same in
> cobol from a C source (this is just a different syntax), paying
> attention to the variable definitions, can't give the same results...

Oh Man, if I had a dollar for every time I've heard someone say that, I 
wouldn't be sitting here typing this. :-)

It is bad enough when a "translation" from one COBOL to another causes 
different results, never mind when a translation from one language to 
another does it. :-)

But you are right. It is reasonable to expect that if the "translation" is 
done carefully, the results SHOULD be identical. I guess we have two 
possible conclusions:

1. The translation wasn't careful enough and something (probably quite 
subtle) was missed.

2. Something is happening at a level we are not normally privy to (like, a 
runtime library, for instance) that is not quite what we expect or want.

It would be possible to take the thing apart and trace through every 
instruction but it is easier to just take a different approach at a higher 
level.

Wrapping it is a good solution.

Thanks for posting what happened.

Pete
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol-C problems

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-08T11:16:19-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6b8cc71e-0812-43d6-9a6e-9d44f12fd542@o9g2000yqa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4f06f44a$0$5034$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`

```
On Jan 7, 2:16 am, Alain Reymond <arwebm...@skynet.be> wrote:
> Hello,
>
> I have problems using a C library under RHEL5, serverexpress 5.
> I installed the libharu library to be able to create pdf files.

I create PDF files for invoices, statements, etc to be emailed but I
wouldn't do it by hard coding it into the program. I do it via a
postscript template and then run ps2pdf.

To draw the template I use tgif (http://bourbon.usc.edu/tgif/
index.html) but several other drawing programs could be used as long
as they output text fields contiguously. To mark the text merge points
I create text fields as: <!TAG> where TAG is the name that I will use
to merge. Several variations are used such as <!TAG---------> to fill
out to the length required, the '-' are ignored, and for multiline
fields:

<!TAG---------->
<!>
<!>

to the number of lines.

I do the merge using a Python program (There was a C program but the
Python one is much faster). The merge data is written out by the Cobol
program (or other) in a text format that I had used since the late 80s
for a commercial DOS package called FormFill which did the merge on a
proprietary graphics format (the design program ran on Windows 2).

This approach has several advantages (to me):
The Postscript can be printed directly via CUPS to any printer.
Or it can be converted to a PDF for emailing.
The format can be quickly and easily changed without changing the
program.
Several different variations can be available just by using a
different template name.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol-C problems

- **From:** Alain Reymond <arwebmail@skynet.be>

In fact, I proceed the same way. I create postscript files from Cobol
and push them via cups on ps printers or as pdf using ps2pdf.
I wrote a few years ago a ps library (http://pscoblib.sourceforge.net/)
in oo cobol that creates postscript files. We use manu graphics in our
reports and it was the easiest way.

Using libharu was just a tentative to see if is possible to write pdf
files using this library. It should be possible as it should be possible
to use the C library pslib (http://pslib.sourceforge.net/). But my
trials were not completely successful until now, although I encounter no
problem writing C programs using both libraries.

As Pete Dashwould said in a previous post :

2. Something is happening at a level we are not normally privy to (like, a runtime library, for instance) that is not quite what we expect or want.

I think he is right!!

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol-C problems

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-09T12:13:25-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<d3d6b5b6-7796-466c-901b-c1e87ea41a89@y2g2000yqk.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4f06f44a$0$5034$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be> <6b8cc71e-0812-43d6-9a6e-9d44f12fd542@o9g2000yqa.googlegroups.com> <4f0aa298$0$5046$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`

```
On Jan 9, 9:17 pm, Alain Reymond <arwebm...@skynet.be> wrote:
> Le 08/01/2012 20:16, Richard a écrit :
>
…[47 more quoted lines elided]…
> and push them via cups on ps printers or as pdf using ps2pdf.

I think that you miss the point. Creating the postscript files or PDF
files by a series of CALLs to a library is _NOT_ 'the same way'.
Templating completely separates the production of the data by the
Cobol program from the presentation. The postscript is created by a
screen design process that even the users can do. The Cobol merely
outputs the data in a simple text file. The merge utility neither
knows nor cares what the data is or what the output is, it just merges
according to simple rules.

The final output could be postscript (or pdf via ps2pdf) or HTML or
XML or simple text and this can be changed completely without changing
the Cobol program at all.


> I wrote a few years ago a ps library (http://pscoblib.sourceforge.net/)
> in oo cobol that creates postscript files. We use manu graphics in our
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> I think he is right!!

It seems to me that your first call of:

    call "HPDF_New" using NULL, NULL returning pdf

is passing the address of 'null' (ie a pointer to NULL) when it should
be (AFAIK) passing a NULL pointer.  Those two NULLs should be 'by
value'.

I haven't looked at any other. You probably should show what hpdf-
types.cpy contains.
```

important tool in their lives (their computer) and it is also at least as 
much fun as playing chess or doing crossword puzzles.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Bloomberg joins the Learn to Code hype

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-01-09T12:03:08+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9mulldFjihU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<8dc6ffd2-b7c4-4709-bccd-85fd8c91516d@ck5g2000vbb.googlegroups.com> <9mt66eFmcpU1@mid.individual.net> <a0c5eb84-82f3-4c92-80b1-73cce3d11ea2@z19g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Jan 8, 9:33 am, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-16440126

Ah, thanks.

Interesting to see that several million started looking at Javascript.

Windows 8 development will be based on XAML and Javascript (primarily) 
although the other languages can also be used. There was a demo of a Windows 
8 app built in minutes using Javascript, CSS, and XAML at the recent MS 
Build conference. The point about this environment is that you can write the 
code once and it runs across all windows platforms, from a desktop machine, 
through Web based devices, to a mobile phone, without change. It is 
accomplished by versions of a framework (runtime) for each platform (very 
similar to, and probably derived from, .Net.)

Over the last few years it has been interesting to see the general public's 
awareness of computing shifting focus from the desktop to the Web. People 
who hear I am involved with computers automatically think I develop Web 
Sites (which I do, but that isn't primarily what I'm doing.) Social 
networking has pervaded the lives of most people (not me...:-)), from kids, 
to Grandparents wanting to keep in touch with their offspring's offspring, 
and it is all accomplished via the Web. There is a generation growing up who 
simply don't recognise a desktop application; it is all cloud based web 
stuff.

In this context it really isn't so foolish to learn Javascript. It is just 
another OO Language. I still prefer ASP.Net for Web development because it 
means I can write C# "code-behinds" which gives my web site full server side 
programming power without the use of a primitive CGI bottleneck (CGI is 
centralised and only multi-threadable with added layers (like ISAPI); C# is 
innately multithreaded and distributed to the pages that require it.) 
However, there is still a place for Client side code and Javascript has 
always been more attractive to me than VBScript for Web programming. Windows 
8 is pushng Javascript to both Client and Server, although you don't HAVE to 
use Javascript for Server side programming.

I also found out recently that kids in High School are now doing "Coding" as 
a unit of their Computer Studies.

It is easy for us to sit back and say:" Well, learning a language doesn't 
make you a programmer." No, it doesn't, but it is a step in the right 
direction and if you write enough code, eventually you will find ways to 
write it better.

Furthermore, the world doesn't have to have millions of expert computer 
programmers. New environments and software development tools are much more 
"forgiving" and much "smarter" than was once the case. Most people who are 
capable of doing a crossword puzzle or solving Sudoku are more than capable 
of tailoring their own personal software for their iPad, phone, or Notebook.

It is just possible that in my own lifetime I will see computing for the 
masses, with people taking control of their devices and without the 
mysterious veil that could only be penetrated by the priests of COBOL...:-) 
I have wanted this since 1965, so it is kind of pleasing to see things 
moving that way.

Pete.
```
